<Date>1559269800107< /Date><Rate>3< /Rate>< review>
The reviews are great and sparked my interest. Perhaps it's busier during lunch time, only one party at 6pm on Thursday.
Buffet consists of mainly chicken leg/thigh, pork, and many types of canned and fresh fruit. It tasted homemade but not impressively tasty. The ceviche though, was very on point.
Price is $13 plus tax and tip.<//review>

<Date>1507424820801< /Date><rating>3< /rating><text>Hello fellow foodies, not real enthused with this place, yet keeping it real once again....

Came in for breakfast with the fam this morning after reading their reviews on Google and Yelp.

Initially observed they could have turned up their airconditioner a bit, it would be more comfortable in there. Considering it was a hot and exceptionally humid morning that extra cooling would have been appreciated.

In all fairness, the food was okay with particular emphasis and kudos on the thinly fried fish referred to as "jeprox". Real satisfying with garlic rice.

The "longanisa" was well seasoned and cooked quite well. Goes down real easy too.

A little dissapointed with the preparation of their "tocino", fried chicken, and adobo as they appeared undercooked and cold. Just couldn't handle more than two or three bites.  (...however in the spirit of fairness, the food looked appetizing in the  warmer.)

I really believe once they get their act together, this place definitely  has tremendous potential.

I will give Bamboo Bistro another try in a few months, and trust that appropriate changes will be made to secure and lock in my business.

See you guys then, I know you can do it guys! See you in a few months.

Thank you!<//text>< Pictures>

<rating>5</rating>< Review>
Budol "fight" style.  Dont let that intimate you. First off, all "dry" food are laid out neatly in the middle of a table covered with banana leaves. If you order saucy or soupy food, it will of course be on a bowl. No utensils unless requested.  The "fight" comes when you sit down and start serving yourself the most delicious Filipino comfort food. There's a convenient sink to wash your hands first.
This is the 2nd Budol fight style restaurant ive been too.  But this one does not need prepaid reservation. Just order off the menu and Happy eating and happy belly!<//Review>

<gmapID>0x80c290d233691303:0x5d0edc5538f824be< /gmapID><response>None< /response><user_id>116957087590985108299<//user_id><rating>5</rating><review>I've been here before for events with the family. It's kind of our go-to place when we dont want to cook Filipino food and worry about clean up afterwards. It's in a interesting location surrounded by Mexican restaurants and stores but it's been going strong within the community for a while and I hope it stays that way.

What's great about Bamboo Bistro is their sense of camaraderie and heritage for Filipino culture. They have karaoke nights, show Filipino television shows and they have "Kamayan" which is the traditional way of eating Filipino food; with your hands.

You don't have to speak tagalog to eat here either, you usually can just point at what looks good and it'll come with a side of rice. Just be weary if you're on a diet since Filipino food is like the Soul Food of Asia.

They also do catering orders *cash only*<//review>< Pictures>

<gmap_id>0x80c290d233691303:0x5d0edc5538f824be< /gmap_id><text>Hands down the best Filipino food in the area!!! You can experience the traditional filipino boodle fight, also known as "kamayan" which is a meal where banana leaves are laid out on the table and the food place down the center, and shared among the party, making it a real communal experience. They also have breakfast and lunch buffets on the weekends which provide an exceptional value for all you can eat Filipino food (I believe $9 for breakfast and $12 for lunch, I know they just increased the price on this recently). Although I have known about this restaurant for more than a year, this was our first time eating at this restaurant. We decided to eat Kamayan style which is the Filipino tradition of eating with your hands.

With Kamayan style, they basically lay banana leaves on the table and they put your food on top of the banana leaves. You use your hands to eat your food. Of course, you cant eat soup with your hands so they do provide you a bowl and a spoon for the soup. We ordered Kare-Kare, Crispy Pata, Talipia, Squid and a couple of other dishes. They were all good!
However, it does take a while to cook the dishes so if you are planning to eat Kamayan style, I would suggest you order before you come in or plan to wait 20-25 minutes for your food to be ready.

The location of the restaurant is in an odd place. It is in a shopping center surrounded by mostly Mexican businesses. It is the only Filipino business in the shopping center.<//text>

This place uses shady sales tactics. We went in looking for hardwood flooring. They added a LOT of square footage to my estimate and were dismissive when I asked them about it. I went back and measured everything myself to show them and suddenly they "lost" the diagram the estimator had drawn up. This place is also NOT a liquadator; they are just a regular old retailer. We needed just barely over 200 square feet of floor underlay and they were going to make us buy a full 300 square feet. If they were a real liquadator they would just sell the extra to someone else. And their claims to be lower priced than other places is complete garbage. We found the same stuff at Lowes for cheaper, with the same labor cost.<//review>

< Review>
They were very well prepared to perform haircuts in a safe and sterile environment. Had to sign up online using their app, and then they would come out to complete the check in with you after receiving the online registration. Wait time said 80+ minutes, but they were much faster than that. Asked how you were feeling, made sure you were wearing a mask and had you sanitize your hands upon entering.
